| **Completely unrelated text** | Likely a hallucination or mis‑interpretation | Discard |

| model‑C            | …          | …                         |
| …                  | …          | …                         |

*If you have more than one model, fill the table. The “Context / Prompt” column helps you verify that every model answered the same question.*

---

## 2️⃣ Normalize the Answers  

1. **Strip formatting** – remove extra whitespace, line‑breaks, markdown, etc.  
2. **Convert to a common datatype** – e.g., if the answer is a number, cast it to an integer/float; if it’s a list, turn it into a Python‑style list; if it’s a paragraph, keep it as a string.  

| Model | Normalized Output |
|-------|-------------------|
| gpt‑oss‑120b | `28` (integer) |
| model‑A      | … |
| model‑B      | … |

---

## 3️⃣ Spot Discrepancies  

| Model | Output | Matches Others? | Notes |
|-------|--------|-----------------|-------|
| gpt‑oss‑120b | 28 | – | Only value so far |
| model‑A      | … | ✅ / ❌ | … |
| model‑B      | … | ✅ / ❌ | … |

*Typical discrepancy patterns*  

| Pattern | What it means | Action |
|---------|---------------|--------|
| **Exact match** across ≥2 models | High confidence | Keep |
| **Minor numeric difference** (e.g., 27 vs 28) | Might be rounding, off‑by‑one, or different interpretation | Check the prompt for units, ranges, or rounding rules |
| **Different data type** (list vs single number) | Could be that one model gave a summary while another gave a raw value | Align to the intended output format |
| **Completely unrelated text** | Likely a hallucination or mis‑interpretation | Discard |

---

## 4️⃣ Validate Against External Knowledge (if possible)  

- **Fact‑check** the numeric answer (e.g., “28” could be a count, a year, a temperature, etc.).  
- Use a trusted source (Wikipedia, official docs, a calculator) to see which model’s answer aligns with reality.  

*Example*: If the question was “How many letters are in the English alphabet?” the correct answer is **26**, so a model output of **28** would be flagged as incorrect.

---

## 5️⃣ Extract the Accurate Components  

1. **Create a “vote tally”** – each model that agrees with the validated answer contributes one vote.  
2. **Select the majority‑voted value** (or the one that matches external verification).  

| Candidate Answer | Votes | External Check |
|------------------|-------|----------------|
| 28               | 1 (so far) | ❓ (needs verification) |
| 26               | 0   | ✅ (official) |
| …                | …   | … |

If the majority (or the verified answer) is **26**, we would discard the `28` from gpt‑oss‑120b.

---

## 6️⃣ Synthesize a Coherent Summary  

- **State the final answer** clearly.  
- **Explain why** that answer was chosen (e.g., “Two out of three models returned 26, and that matches the official count of letters in the alphabet.”).  
- **Mention any discarded information** only if it helps the reader understand the reasoning.  

**Template**

> **Answer:** *|final value or statement]*  
> **Rationale:** The majority of models (X out of Y) produced *|value]*, which aligns with *|trusted source]*. The outlier(s) (*e.g., 28 from gpt‑oss‑120b*) differed because *|reason]*, so they were excluded.

- **Convert units** if needed (e.g., “40 km”, “40 miles” → decide on a common unit).

| “four‑zero” (text) | model‑B | Z |

- **Agreement**: If ≥ 2 models give the same normalized answer, treat it as a *candidate truth*.
- **Discrepancy**: Any answer that appears only once (or with a minority) is flagged for further scrutiny.

---

## 4️⃣ Evaluate the Credibility of Each Model  

| Model | Known Strengths | Known Weaknesses | Recent Performance on Similar Tasks |
|-------|----------------|------------------|--------------------------------------|
| gpt‑oss‑120b | Good at arithmetic, open‑source fine‑tuned | Smaller parameter count than GPT‑4 | 95 % correct on simple numeric Q&A |
| model‑A | Strong reasoning, but sometimes “hallucinates” numbers | … | 88 % |
| model‑B | … | … | … |

Weight each model’s vote by its reliability score (e.g., 0.95 for gpt‑oss‑120b, 0.88 for model‑A). Compute a **weighted majority** if needed.

---

## 5️⃣ Extract the “Accurate Components”  

- **Numeric core**: The number itself (e.g., 40).  
- **Units / qualifiers**: If any model adds “seconds”, “percent”, etc., keep only those that are consistent across the majority.  
- **Contextual explanation**: If a model supplies a short justification that matches the majority reasoning, retain it; discard contradictory or unsupported explanations.

---

## 6️⃣ Eliminate the Incorrect or Unreliable Parts  

- Remove any answer that appears only in low‑credibility models **and** conflicts with the weighted majority.  
- Discard extraneous text that does not pertain to the question (e.g., “I think the answer might be 40, but I'm not sure”).  
- If a model adds a unit that no other model mentions, verify the original prompt; if the unit is unsupported, drop it.

---

## 7️⃣ Synthesize a Coherent Summary  

1. **State the consensus answer** (with confidence).  
2. **Explain why this answer is preferred** (agreement, model reliability).  
3. **Note any remaining ambiguity** (e.g., “If the question required a unit, the prompt did not specify one, so we assume a plain number”).  
4. **Provide a concise rationale** (optional, based on the majority explanation).
